The moments that moved Pelosi and House Democrats toward impeachment.'"><span class="social-lbl">Email </span><i class="fa fa-envelope"></i></a> <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/people/kevin-uhrmacher/"><span>Bio</span> <i class="fa fa-external-link-alt"></i></a> <a href="https://twitter.com/KevinUhrm">Follow <i class="fa fa-twitter"></i> </a> </div> </div> </div> </div> </div> </div> <span class="author-timestamp" content="2019-09-25T01:07-500" itemprop="datePublished">September 25 at 1:07 AM</span> </div> <p data-elm-loc="0">Rep. Al Green, Democrat of Texas, was a maverick when he started <a href="https://washpost.arcpublishing.com/pb/news/powerpost/wp/2017/12/05/democratic-rep-al-green-says-he-will-force-house-impeachment-vote/">trying to impeach</a> President Trump in 2017. Tuesday, his party took that remarkable step formally, when House Speaker Nancy Pelosi announced an impeachment inquiry into the president. Close to <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/graphics/2019/politics/impeachment-support-house-democrats/">200 House Democrats</a> now are openly supportive of that investigation, following rapidly developing news that Trump had talked to the president of Ukraine about investigating a political opponent  and withheld nearly $400 million in aid from the country.</p> <p data-elm-loc="1">In between, Democratic support for an impeachment inquiry has grown in fits and starts, often corresponding to key junctures in the many investigations of the 45th president, including that of Special Counsel Robert S. Mueller III.</p> <div class="inline-content inline-html" data-elm-loc="2"> <div class="pg-graphic fallback-available" The report detailed <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/graphics/2019/politics/mueller-obstruction-evidence/" target="_blank">10 instances of possible obstruction of justice</a> by Trump, setting off a firestorm in the Democratic caucus. Soon after its release, many more members from safe Democratic districts announced their support. Among those were the other members of the squad who signed onto Tlaibs resolution.</p> <p data-elm-loc="13">During this time period, the administration also blocked former White House Counsel Don McGahn from testifying in relation to the report, saying he was absolutely immune from compelled congressional testimony. Several lawmakers came out for impeachment in the following days.</p> <p data-elm-loc="14">Pelosi allies and moderates mostly preferred additional investigations over impeachment proceedings at this point, as the speaker said <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/were-not-there-yet-pelosi-pushes-back-on-impeachment-as-more-democrats-call-for-proceedings/2019/04/23/51639b48-65e9-11e9-8985-4cf30147bdca_story.html" target="_blank">if the ... fact-finding takes us there, we have no choice. But were not there yet.</a></p> <p data-elm-loc="15">Mueller kicked the impeachment ball to the Congress. The Constitution gives the responsibility to Congress to impeach an unfit president  high crimes and misdemeanors. What more do we need? Rep. In the statement, Mueller cited Justice Department policy for his inability to charge Trump, tossing the matter to Congress and <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/muellers-statement-increases-pressure-on-pelosi-to-begin-trump-impeachment/2019/05/29/60e8ec5c-8228-11e9-933d-7501070ee669_story.html" target="_blank">upping the pressure on Pelosi</a>.</p> <p data-elm-loc="21">Many constituents want to impeach the president. Bennie Thompson (Miss.) <a href="https://www.wgbh.org/news/politics/2019/05/29/mcgovern-responds-to-mueller-we-have-to-do-whats-right" target="_blank">said</a>, in pushing for impeachment proceedings.</p> <h2 data-elm-loc="23">Following the Mueller testimony</h2> <h6 data-elm-loc="24">Mid-July to mid-September</h6> <div class="inline-content inline-html" data-elm-loc="25"> <div class="pg-graphic fallback-available" Reps. Chris Pappas (N.H.) and Lauren Underwood (Ill.) were the first to do so.</p> <p data-elm-loc="27">One of them was Rep. John Garamendi (Calif.), who, in an interview with The Post on July 25, compared an inquiry to grand jury proceedings. First, open an impeachment inquiry, he said, then we will see where we go with an impeachment, a formal resolution.</p> <p data-elm-loc="28">That same day, Trump spoke with Ukrainian President Volodymyr Zelensky. His conversation would emerge in a whistleblower complaint filed in August. The Post has reported that Trump urged Ukraine to investigate former vice president and 2020 presidential candidate Joe Biden and his son Hunter as the administration was holding up congressional appropriations of military and intelligence aid.</p> <p data-elm-loc="29">Hunter Biden served for nearly five years on the board of Burisma, Ukraines largest private gas company, whose owner came under scrutiny by Ukrainian prosecutors for possible abuse of power and unlawful enrichment. Hunter Biden was not accused of any wrongdoing in the investigation. As vice president, Joe Biden pressured Ukraine to fire the top prosecutor, Viktor Shokin, who Biden and other Western officials said was not sufficiently pursuing corruption cases. At the time, the investigation into Burisma was dormant, according to former Ukrainian and U.S. officials.</p> <p data-elm-loc="30">By that time, the House Judiciary Committee had started an investigation into whether it would recommend articles of impeachment against Trump.</p> <p data-elm-loc="31">Rep. Jerrold Nadler (D-N.Y.), chairman of the Judiciary Committee and a Pelosi ally, confirmed the probe in an Aug. 8 interview with CNN and is likely to oversee the impeachment inquiry announced Tuesday.</p> <h2 data-elm-loc="32">As the whistleblower story broke</h2> <h6 data-elm-loc="33">Mid-September, as of 10 p.m. Tuesday</h6> <div class="inline-content inline-html" data-elm-loc="34"> <div Several have backgrounds in national security.</p> <p data-elm-loc="36">The president of the United States may have used his position to pressure a foreign country into investigating a political opponent, and he sought to use U.S. taxpayer dollars as leverage to do it, seven freshman Democrats from competitive districts <a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/opinions/2019/09/24/seven-freshman-democrats-these-allegations-are-threat-all-we-have-sworn-protect/" target="_blank">wrote in a Post op-ed backing an inquiry</a>. They were among the dozens of lawmakers who moved to yes in a 24-hour span.</p> <p data-elm-loc="37">There comes a time when you have to be moved by the spirit of history to take action to protect and preserve the integrity of our nation. I believe, I truly believe, the time to begin impeachment proceedings against this president has come, Rep. John Lewis (Ga.), a close Pelosi ally who had long remained quiet on the matter, said on the House floor. To delay or to do otherwise would betray the foundation of our democracy.</p> <p data-elm-loc="38">On Tuesday, amid mounting pressure from all sides of her caucus, Pelosi took the step she had long avoided.</p> <p data-elm-loc="39"><b>About this story</b></p> <p data-elm-loc="40"><i>The Fix </i><a href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/graphics/2019/politics/impeachment-support-house-democrats/" target="_blank"><i>impeachment tally</i></a><i> compiled by JM Rieger. 2016 election results from Dave Leips U.S. Election Atlas.
